In pursuance of the different orders of authorisation (15) granted by the Public Health and Housing Committee, it has not been found necessary to institute legal proceedings in any case for the abatement of nuisances and non-compliance with the London County Council's and Poplar Borough Council's own bye-laws, as the nuisances were satisfactorily abated previous to applying for summonses. Milk Shops and Milk Sellers. I have by your instructions made periodical inspections of premises where milk is stored and sold throughout the district with the objectof enforcing the regulations of the "Dairies, Cowsheds and Milkshops Order of 1885,"as amended by the Dairies, Cowsheds and Milkshops Amending Order of 1886, and the London County Council (General Powers) Act, 1908, Section 5 (Milk Clauses), in respect to the sanitary condition of the premises, cleanliness of measures, counter pans, means of storage, and prevention of contamination, particularly in respect to other articles kept for sale in the same premises; where old measures were found to be in use (porous) new ones have been provided, also where the counter pans were not properly covered instructions were given to have proper ones provided. Five notices were received for renewal of licences. The premises were duly inspected in respect to the necessary cleansing and limewashing, which has been done in accordance with the provisions of the Dairy and Cowsheds Order, any defects found were remedied before the licences were granted. The slaughterhouses have been frequently visited, and at times when killing was in progress, and everything found satisfactory. The number of these premises now on the register are—cowsheds, 2; slaughterhouses, 3. Q 230 Overcrowding. During the year only four complaints of overcrowding were received; in each case the nuisances were abated after the service of intimation and statutory notices without recourse to legal proceedings. Ice Cream Manufacturers and Itinerant Vendors. All the premises where ice cream is made have been inspected with the view of detecting nuisances, also any infringement of the London County Council's (General Powers) Act, 1902, Part viii. Each itinerant vendor's barrow and utensils have been inspected. In each case the manufacturer's name was found to be legibly affixed thereto, the ice cream and utensils were found to be satisfactory, no cause for action to be taken. Cleansing of Cisterns (Bye-laws wider Section 50). The cisterns of the undermentioned buildings have been inspected during the year, and duly reported upon. Where covers were found to be defective, have since been amended, and made as far as practicable dustproof. Each cistern is so situated as to be free from pollution:— Adelaide Buildings 2, Baffins Buildings 2, Grosvenor Buildings 55, Hudson's Buildings 2, Melbourne Buildings 4, Montreal Buildings 4, Ontario Buildings 4, Ottawa Buildings 4, Prestage Buildings 6, Quebec Buildings 4, Council Buildings 5, St. Lawrence Cottages, Norfolk Street 14, Sydney Buildings 4, Toronto Buildings 2, Winnipeg Buildings 4. Outworkers. The premises where male outworkers live and work have been inspected, and notices to cleanse the premises have been served where required. London County Council (General Powers) Act, 1904, Section 20. During the year, on inspection, 12 rooms were found to be in a verminous condition. Intimations, also Statutory Notices where necessary were served, and the nuisances satisfactorily abated, without recourse to legal proceedings. 231 Coffee Houses, Restaurants, Private Hotels, Sausage Makers, Fried Fish Shops, etc. Periodical inspection has been given to these premises during the past year; change of proprietorship, new premises opened and those closed have been duly reported and noted in the register. At each inspection particular attention was paid to the food being prepared, and in no instance was there cause for complaint; in some cases it was necessary to serve intimations and statutory notices respecting cleansing of the kitchens, etc. Hairdressers' Shops. The whole of the hairdressers' shops throughout my district have been inspected, the sanitary condition of the premises, cleanliness of the articles used in the business being carefully noted. In some few cases intimations were required. Generally there is a marked improvement in these premises since they have been periodically inspected. Public House Urinals. The public house urinals have been under regular observation during the past year, and the London County Council (General Powers) Act, 1904, Section 22, strictly enforced. Canal Boats. The inspection of canal boats was without particular incident during the year. Factory and Workshops Acts. The workshops, domestic workshops, workplaces and domestic workplaces in the district where male labour is employed have been inspected, the number employed in each case being checked, particularly in respect to overcrowding, the terms of the Acts relating thereto have been met with in response to intimation and statutory notices when necessary, and in no instance has occasion required legal proceedings. Smoke Nuisances. During the year the shafts throughout the district have been under careful observation, and in only two instances nuisances were detected. In these cases intimations and statutory notices have been 232 served, which has had the desired effect of abating the nuisances. No recurrence of the nuisances taking place, and no necessity to take legal proceedings. Unsound Food, Shops and Stalls. The shops and stalls in the district have been frequently inspected in respect of unsound and unwholesome food, and during the past year there has been no occasion to seize any article exposed for sale. During the year two cases of conger eels, ten baskets of cherries and one case of skate were brought to the Public Health Offices to be examined, and were found to be unfit for human food. After the usual precautions being taken to prevent any abuse of the condemnation, the usual certificate was given for the purpose of the purchaser getting his money from the wholesale vendor. Riverside Wharves where Food is Stored, etc. There is only one wharf in my district, viz., Concordia Wharf, Cold Harbour (Ramornie Meat Co.), where food (all tinned) is landed, some of which is warehoused for other firms; the other, which is all examined, is for sale for both home consumption and export. A large amount goes into the Mercantile Service, all of which is examined and duly labelled by their officials before being taken away. The following number of tinned food (as set out below) on examination were found to be blown or otherwise damaged and consequently condemned as unfit for human food, which were set apart in a building adjoining these premises for the purpose of being sent to a fat boiler to be rendered down for fat. Proper precautions have been taken to prevent the condemned food being used for any other purpose. 293 61bs. beef, 323 21bs. beef, 21 llb. beef, 3 21bs. steak, 1 2ilb. steak, 9 21bs. sausages, 32 21bs. soup, 4 21bs. tongue, 2 llb. tongue, 1,043 61bs. mutton, 168 21bs. mutton, 32 l½lbs. chicken—making a total of 1,931 tins. The "Regulations under the Public Health (Regulations as to Food) Act, 1907," give more power to your Inspecctor to inspect food imported into this country, and which will facilitate a more rigid examination, also supervision of the disposal of unsound food. 233 Public Schools. I have, as specially instructed, inspected the Public Schools in my district, particularly in respect to the water supply and sanitary conveniences. The water supply for drinking purposes at each school was found to be drawn from the rising main, and the storage cisterns are cleansed periodically. The sanitary conveniences and offices were found to be in a clean and satisfactory condition. I am, Sir, Your obedient Servant, JAMES BULLOCK, Sanitary Inspector, Inspector under the Sale of Food and Drugs Acts and Inspector of Canal Boats, East Combined Division. 234 Report of Inspector, South Division of Poplar. Inspections, special, periodical and on complaint of nuisances 1,072 Inspections re notifications of infectious diseases 266 Inspections, house-to-house visitations 133 Total Inspections 1,471 Re-inspections 3,390 House-to-House Inspections. The number of complaints with reference to black smoke issuing from the numerous factory chimney shafts in Millwall and Cubitt Town have been considerably less during the past year. The nuisances occurring were in most cases abated on the service of an intimation, and when necessary followed by a statutory notice. In one instance only was it necessary to resort to legal proceedings.* The smoke-preventing appliances attached to many of the furnaces, in conjunction with careful stoking, as the result of previous proceedings, rep sated visits, and cautions, no doubt contributed to this result. * See Legal Proceedings under Public Health Acts. 238 Inspection of Schools. Local Street, Alpha Ed. Man. Act, 1855. Dismissed; no costs allowed. In the above case the summons was dismissed on a technical legal point relating to ownership. For the defence it was held that in this particular instance the responsible person must be not only freeholder of the court but also owner of the adjacent premises as interpreted by Sec. 99 of the Metropolis Local Management Act, 1855, and as these premises were held under long leases by different owners, who were not the freeholders of the cul de sac, the freeholder could not be held responsible for the work. With this the magistrate concurred. Premises where Food Stuffs were Sold or Prepared for Sale. Maconochie's Wharf and Food Manufacturing and Preserving Factory, West Ferry Road. The above premises were constantly visited during the year. Particular attention was paid to the various food stuffs in course of preparation, as well as to the cleanliness of the vessels and utensils in use and of the sanitary conditions generally of the different kitchens and preparing rooms. All unsound or tainted food stuffs, blown or suspicious tinned food, etc., were destroyed in the furnaces by the firm on the premises, mostly in my presence. Summary of food stuffs destroyed during the year at this factory, all of which was contained in tins varying from ½lb. to 141bs. in weight:— Fish (mixed), principally lobster, salmon, cod, and herring 365 tins Meat, including meat paste 502 ,, Vegetable (various) 34 ,, Fruit (various) 49 „ Mixed fish, meat, and fruit 29 „ Total 979 tins 241 With reference to food stuffs exported to foreign countries, viz., the Philippine Islands (where certificates were required to accompany each consignment from the Sanitary Authority of the district whence the goods were dispatched), the premises were visited and the factory inspected and the goods examined and reported satisfactory before the certificates were signed by yourself. Sufferance Wharf and Food Preserving and Manufacturing Premises (for export only), West Ferry Road, Millwall. These premises were frequently visited and all unsound food stuffs, suspicious or blown tinned foods (sorted from imported stock) were destroyed by the firm. Summary of food stuffs examined and destroyed:- 70 cases tinned fish, mixed, principally lobster, salmon and sardines, about 50 tins per case. 469 tins mixed goods, fish and vegetables. 15 tins meat. 53 tins vegetables. 2 tons ½ cwt. of lemon skins. 25 cases of fish paste, previously condemned at the docks, were permitted by the Port Sanitary Authority to be delivered at the above premises for examination. On the application of the firm to yourself, permission was also given for the further removal of the goods to their factory at Lowestoft, and the medical officer of that district was notified of their despatch. Frequent exportations from this factory of consignments of hams or tinned meat to the Argentine or Philippines (where a certificate is required from the Sanitary Authority of the district whence the goods are despatched to accompany each consignment) had occurred. In every instance the factory had been visited and the goods examined before the certificates were signed. The additional powers conferred by the Regulations under the Public Health Regulations as to Food Act, 1907, will greatly facilitate in future a more rigid inspection of food stuffs landed at the above-mentioned wharves, and a more effectual means of dealing with and disposing of unsound food is defined in that statute. 242 The shops and stalls in the main thoroughfares were regularly visited. Surprise visits were made frequently on Saturday nights and occasionally on Sunday mornings. Although several small articles were destroyed as suspicious or tainted, in no instance was I justified in seizing any food stuff exposed for sale during these visits. Food Stuff Surrendered. During the year, at the request of the owners, 5 dozen frozen rabbits and ½cwt. trunk of fish were examined and found to be unfit for human food. Certificates to that effect were given to the owners after the goods were destroyed. Sale of Food and Drugs Acts. Fifty-seven samples of food and drugs were purchased and submitted to the Public Analyst for analysis. Of that number 4 contained boric acid preservatives in the proportions of .2, .3, .5, and .8 per cent. respectively. In the last instance, viz., sample containing .8 per cent., legal proceedings were instituted. Of the remaining samples taken 6 were certified to be so adulterated that summonses were issued against the respective vendors, and in one case (sample marked 2F, butter certified to contain 80 5 per cent. foreign fat) butter was asked for and charged for at the rate of 1s. per lb., but as it was handed to the purchaser in a wrapper stamped margarine legal proceedings were not advised. The nature of samples and extent of adulteration, with result of prosecutions, are indicated below:- 6F Butter—Adulterated with 62.6 per cent. of foreign fat. Vendor fined £2 and £1 3s. costs 24F Butter—Adulterated with 81.1 per cent. foreign fat. Summons withdrawn through error in analyst's certificate. 30s. paid to vendor for cost of analysis. 32F Milk—Deficient in fat 10 per cent. Dismissed, no costs allowed. In this case the defence proved by expert evidence to the satisfaction of the Court that the milk when sold was in the same condition as when taken from their own cow, and had not been tampered with. 34F Milk—Deficient in solids not fat 9.4 per cent. Vendor fined £1 and £1 3s. costs. The written warranty defence failed. 243 45F Milk —Deficient in solids not fat 4 7 per cent. £1 and £1 3s. costs. 52F Butter—Contained .8 per cent. of boric acid. £1 and 12s. 6d. co3ts. This is one of the first convictions obtained through the excessive use of a preservative. Public Health Department, December 31st, 1908. To the Medical Officer of Health. Sir,— I beg to present my ninth Annual Report which deals with the work done in factories, workshops, among outworkers and other miscellaneous inspections during 1908. During the year one notice was served where the sanitary accommodation was unsuitable, and one where it was not separate for the sexes; in each case satisfactory alterations were made. Scabies and Verminous Children. I have visited a number of houses from which children were excluded from school when suffering from scabies, or on account of their verminous condition, and have had bedding disinfected and cleansing carried out. Inspection of Schools. The sanitary accommodation in the whole of the elementary schools in the Borough has been inspected and various defects referred to the London County Council. Outworkers. The outworkers' lists have been inspected at the premises from which work was given out, and 147 lists have been received from employers in the Borough; 319 lists have been forwarded from other Boroughs containing the names of persons who live in Poplar; 324 lists have been sent to other Councils containing the names of persons who work for employers in Poplar. Prosecutions. Two employers were prosecuted for not sending in their lists as required. One was fined, and the other summons adjourned sine die. Rothbury Road. 248 Special Report re Legal Proceedings. In March last the special attention of the Council was drawn to a report by the Medical Officer of Health on "Legal Proceedings under the Bye-laws," concerning some houses in Beachy Road, Old Ford. Briefly the facts were as follows:- The houses were in a dirty and verminous condition, and the owner, who did not comply with notices, was summoned to Old Street Police Court before Mr. Cluer. The magistrate heard the evidence of the Medical Officer of Health and myself, and although the owner did not dispute the condition of the rooms, and could offer no rebutting evidence, the magistrate decided to allow further time for the work to be done, and upon the completion of the work the magistrate withdrew the summonses and refused to allow the Council any costs. A report at the time after the magistrate's action was presented by the Medical Officer of Health, first to the Committee and then to the Council. San. Insp. Exam. Board (Land.) Sanitary Inspector and Inspector of Houses Let in Lodgings. 250 Report of Health Visitor. Public Health Offices, January lst, 1909. Sir,— The following is a Report of my work during the year 1908. I commenced my duties on May 4th, my time being chiefly occupied in trying to gain interest in the formation of a Voluntary Helpers Association. I, of necessity, met with some opposition, but that the idea was generally accepted with favour was shown, when at a meeting held on June 1st, only one month after I commenced my duties, it was unanimously decided that an Association, having for its object the prevention of infantile mortality, should be formed in the Borough. Since then the work has gone steadily forward, until at the time of writing, the Association has some sixty members, visiting from one to thirty-five babies each. Five "Centres'' have been formed in the Borough, each Centre having its own Hon. Sec., Committee and Band of Helpers, from members of which the Executive Committee (which is the governing body of the Association) is formed. Monthly "Consultation Days for Mothers and Babies" have been established in three "Centres."* Here fully qualified medical women (whose services are honorary) attend to give advice on the feeding, etc., of both infant and mother, and the infants are also weighed. I regret that so far my efforts to get a "Nursing Mothers' Milk Fund" established have been unsuccessful. Much good would be done in this way if the Guardians, when giving relief to a nursing mother, would see that due proportion was given in the form of milk and oatmeal, and in the case of a mother unable to suckle her child, a proper supply of milk for the infant. The organisation of an Association like this of necessity takes up a large amount of time, and as the Voluntary Helpers' reports are received every four weeks, the clerical work entailed is considerable and leaves me but little time for actual visiting. I am strongly of opinion that each case ought to be visited first by a trained worker, and those requiring systematic visiting, handed on, by her, to the Voluntary Helper. With only one trained worker, this is, of course, impossible. *A consultation day in a fourth centre has been established at the beginning of 1909. 251 Coming to the actual work, 3,495 visits have been paid to 832 babies. This number does not include "outs." Twelve of these had died before the visit took place; thirty-one have died since, and eighty-nine have removed. Reliable statistics regarding the whole are not available. The work of the Voluntary Helpers is most valuable, but one can hardly expect them, at any rate as yet, to gain the same amount of information as a trained worker. The following figures, however, relating to those families systematically visited by myself may prove interesting and may also be taken as typical of the whole:— Visited 336 Removed 39 Died 15 Taking away the thirty-nine who removed, this gives a death-rate of 50.5 per 1000 visited. Of those remaining, there were— 223 breast fed. 56 mixed feeding. 3 hand fed. The mothers of these infants had previously given birth to 1224 living children, of whom 187 died before reaching the age of one year, giving an infantile mortality rate of 152.7 per 1000 births. 26.6 per cent. worked for varying periods during pregnancy, 15.4 per cent. have started work since the birth of the child. Very few work regularly, so that reliable information as to income is hard to obtain, but amongst the home-workers the average earnings appears to be 1s. per day, and in some cases this is not earned without the help of the children. 15 per cent. have, at some period of my visits, been in receipt of parish relief. 21 per cent. occupied only one room; 25 per cent. two rooms, the families often consisting of parents and five children, and even where two rooms are occupied, the same sleeping apartment serves for all. If the authorities compel them to move, it is only to come across them later on, living under similar conditions. Of the fifteen deaths: — 2 died in the 1st month. 5 „ 2nd „ 4 „ 3rd „ 1 „ 4th „ 3 „ 5th „ 252 The causes of death were:— Inanition, marasmus, etc. (6 being twin children) 8 Convulsions 4 Epidemic diarrhœa 2 Heart failure 1 The method of feeding:— Breast fed 7 Mixed feeding 7 Hand fed 1 The last being fed from birth on separated condensed milk. Three of the mothers worked both during pregnancy and after the birth of the child. Two during pregnancy only. The difference in the rate of mortality between the infants of working and non-working mothers being shown in the following table:— Non-working mothers 4.8 per cent. Worked during pregnancy 6.7 „ Worked both during pregnancy and after birth of child 6.9 ,, The conditions of home life in three cases were decidedly unsatisfactory. In conclusion, will you allow me to take this opportunity of thanking all those who have helped to build up the Voluntary Helpers' Association, especially those who give up so much of their time to visiting the homes of their less fortunate sisters, to whom their sympathy and friendly advice means so much. I have the honour to remain, Sir, Your obedient Servant, ALICE E. HALL. Cert. San. Insp. Exam. Board (Lond.) Associate R. San. Inst. Cert. Lond. Obst. Society. Registered Central Midwives Board.
